> **2026-05-02 — ORCH-0708 NEW (S1) — Wave 2 Phase 1 photo-aesthetic scoring integration. Forensics + spec landed. Awaits implementor dispatch.** First Wave 2 deliverable. Auditable evidence from live Mingla-dev DB proves 5 structural limits in current scoring: (R-1) cap=200 squashes 5–7% of dining places at top — 2,620 places stuck at exactly 200 across casual_food / brunch / drinks / icebreakers; (R-2) popularity dominates 38–74% of every top-decile score, drowning quality differentiation; (R-3) text-pattern matching only fires for 3.6% of fine_dining places — 96.4% of the 50-point text budget is wasted; (R-4) NULL Google booleans devastate stale cities (London/Brussels/Baltimore = 100% NULL on serves_dinner/reservable/dine_in/wine/generative_summary; even DC/Raleigh/Cary/Durham/FL = 53–73% NULL); (R-5) per-city quality drift confirms ORCH-0702 (Baltimore p90 fine_dining=61.4 vs FL p90=109.7) — global filter_min is structurally wrong. **Architectural fix:** new `place_pool.photo_aesthetic_data jsonb` column owned EXCLUSIVELY by new `score-place-photo-aesthetics` edge function; 7 new JSONB-aware field-weight prefix matchers (`photo_aesthetic_above_X`, `photo_lighting_X`, `photo_composition_X`, `photo_subject_X`, `photo_vibe_includes_X`, `photo_appropriate_for_includes_X`, `photo_inappropriate_for_includes_X`, `photo_safety_includes_X`) extend signalScorer.ts (~70 LOC); 7 v_next signal config migrations adding photo-derived weights + raising cap 200→1000 on fine_dining, brunch, romantic, lively, casual_food, drinks, icebreakers; cap stays at 200 on the other 9 signals. **Asymmetric weight design** (§19 of spec) — photo data captured ONCE per place via Claude Haiku 4.5 vision call, scored DIFFERENTLY per signal. Same JSONB blob produces +170 in fine_dining and -100 in icebreakers for an upscale candle-lit place. Bidirectional misclassification fix (corrects false positives AND false negatives, including the Baltimore-NULL-boolean famine and the Trapeze-class promiscuity). **Cost:** ~$11 for Raleigh+Cary+Durham (3,234 places) at Haiku batch+cache, well under $200 escalation. **Prompt safeguards (7 layers, §20):** calibration examples baked in system prompt (6 anchored cases A–F covering upscale/brunch/dive/strip-club/storefront/coffeeshop) · anti-hedging rule · honest-grading rule · inappropriate_for discipline rule · `dry_run_sample` action for 30-place pre-flight at $0.10 per iter · 10 golden test fixtures (§22) · disagreement logging via new `photo_aesthetic_unknown_outputs` table. **Sonnet 4.6 escalation hatch (§21, optional flag)** for safety-flagged low-confidence places. **2 new invariants queued for CLOSE:** I-PHOTO-AESTHETIC-DATA-SOLE-OWNER + I-PHOTO-AESTHETIC-CACHE-FINGERPRINT (sha256 of stored_photo_urls.slice(0,5) drives idempotent skip on re-run). **Architectural constraint locked:** lives INSIDE current scoring system per `memory/project_place_intelligence_architecture.md`; NOT a replacement. Operator's stated UX target met: after deploy, "just run scoring again" works (one curl per signal). **6 discoveries:** D-INV-1 per-city percentile (Option C from cap decision) → ORCH-0709 candidate · D-INV-2 filter_min re-tune review during CLOSE · D-INV-3 unknown vibe_tags log table (folded into spec §20.7) · D-INV-4 London/Brussels/Lagos/Baltimore need admin-refresh-places (parallel ORCH item) · D-INV-5 AI columns still in schema despite memory-flagged decommission · D-INV-6 signal_definition_versions UNIQUE constraint still missing from ORCH-0702. **ID collision history:** ORCH-0704 → ORCH-0706 → ORCH-0708 (three collisions in one drafting session — pattern lesson for future orchestrator sessions: re-grep the ORCH counter at the top of every registration step, not just at SPEC drafting). **Files:** [reports/INVESTIGATION_ORCH-0708_SCORING_SYSTEM_AUDIT.md](Mingla_Artifacts/reports/INVESTIGATION_ORCH-0708_SCORING_SYSTEM_AUDIT.md) · [reports/SPEC_ORCH-0708_PHOTO_AESTHETIC_SCORING_INTEGRATION.md](Mingla_Artifacts/reports/SPEC_ORCH-0708_PHOTO_AESTHETIC_SCORING_INTEGRATION.md) · [prompts/FORENSICS_ORCH-0708_PHOTO_AESTHETIC_SCORING_AUDIT_AND_SPEC.md](Mingla_Artifacts/prompts/FORENSICS_ORCH-0708_PHOTO_AESTHETIC_SCORING_AUDIT_AND_SPEC.md). **Status:** REVIEW APPROVED 10/10 · IMPL dispatch ready · awaits operator `/mingla-implementor` invocation. **Active queue post-this-entry:** ORCH-0708 IMPL dispatch ready (operator runs `/mingla-implementor`); ORCH-0709 (per-city percentile) deferred to Wave 2 follow-up cycle after ORCH-0708 ships; ORCH-0700 SPEC v2 still blocked on operator decisions; PR #59 ORCH-0706 + ORCH-0707 in their own queues.

> **2026-05-01 — ORCH-0700 FORENSICS RETURNED + REVIEW APPROVED 10/10 → SPEC DISPATCH PENDING 5 OPERATOR STRATEGIC DECISIONS.** Investigation: [reports/INVESTIGATION_ORCH-0700_MOVIES_CHIP_LEAK.md](Mingla_Artifacts/reports/INVESTIGATION_ORCH-0700_MOVIES_CHIP_LEAK.md). 11 sections, file:line citations to every leak step, full five-truth-layer table, pattern-class assessment. **Layman truth:** the canonical post-OTA Movies chip does NOT silently swap in theatres at the routing layer (G1 H confidence). Two real holes exist: (1) the legacy `'Movies & Theatre'` union path serving theatre venues with `displayCategory: 'Movies'` to any pre-OTA client until [TRANSITIONAL] exit 2026-05-13 — 12 days; (2) the curated-stop replacement path queries `ai_categories CONTAINS 'movies_theatre'` rather than canonical type list, returning AI-tagged theatres. A third surface: Marbles IMAX (science museum) is shipping today as a Movies card because the soft scorer's reviews regex matches "theater" — operator must decide if intentional or a leak. **Architectural root cause (one-paragraph):** `displayCategory` is computed at routing layer (CATEGORY_TO_SIGNAL) from chip-tapped intent, not derived from row's `primary_type` at emission time. This fabrication is visible only when routing intent diverges from row's actual type — happens any time a union mapping exists, any time soft scorer lets a non-canonical type clear filter_min, and any time a downstream surface reads `displayCategory` rather than `primary_type` to render the category badge. Person-hero already uses the correct pattern at `get-person-hero-cards/index.ts:109` (`mapPrimaryTypeToMinglaCategory(raw.primary_type, raw.types ?? [])`); discover-cards does NOT — Constitution #2 violation between two parallel card-serving paths. The structural fix is to derive `category` from row's `primary_type` at emission time, making `displayCategory` a routing-only concept that never reaches the rendered card. Without this, every future chip split, every union mapping, and every relaxed filter_min reopens the same leak class. **Pattern-class CONFIRMED, not Movies-only:** identical architecture leaks for the legacy `'Brunch, Lunch & Casual'` `[TRANSITIONAL]` union at `discover-cards/index.ts:90-91` (signalIds `['brunch','casual_food']` + `displayCategory: 'Brunch'` — exit 2026-05-12) and is the same shape every narrow chip will hit if its scorer relaxes. Movies is the most exposed because of smallest universe (7 cinemas Raleigh) + most permissive filter_min (80 vs 120 default). **6 discoveries triaged:** D-OBS-1 (replace-curated-stop VALID_CATEGORIES locked to legacy slugs — needs canonical Movies/Theatre/Brunch/Casual added) · D-OBS-2 (`place_pool.ai_categories` never migrated post-ORCH-0598 — separate ORCH candidate for AI re-categorisation pipeline run) · D-OBS-3 (`DISPLAY_TO_SLUG` missing canonical Movies/Theatre keys → `mapCategoryToSlug('Movies')` returns empty string; today tolerated by mobile, future surfaces may not) · D-OBS-4 (`CATEGORY_EXCLUDED_PLACE_TYPES` missing canonical Movies/Theatre entries — affects on-demand experience generation, not Discover deck signal RPC) · D-OBS-5 (Marbles IMAX shipping as Movies — A3 confirmed live; operator decides intentional vs leak) · D-PROC-1 (Constitution #2 enforcement gap on taxonomy splits — three code paths kept pre-split logic and now disagree; recommend spec-review template addition) · D-PROC-2 (taxonomy-split migrations must touch ALL columns of all tables, not just user-facing ones — recommend migration review checklist addition). **4 invariants violated:** INV-Exclusion-Consistency · INV-Source-of-Truth-Single (Constitution #2) · INV-No-Fabricated-Data (Constitution #9) · INV-Solo-Collab-Parity (holds via G8 — both modes leak identically; honesty property not defect). **5 strategic operator decisions required before SPEC dispatch:** (Q1) A1 timing — fix now via structural fix vs let [TRANSITIONAL] cleanup at 2026-05-13 handle it · (Q2) A3 Marbles IMAX semantics — intentional broad cinema-experience surfacing vs hard type-gate enforcement · (Q3) architectural depth — full structural fix (derive category from primary_type at emission) vs surgical patch (close A1+A2 without unifying the architecture) · (Q4) pattern-class scope — fix Movies as wedge proving architecture vs sweep all narrow chips (Brunch/Casual same exposure) · (Q5) D-OBS-2 ai_categories migration — full AI re-categorisation pipeline run (~hours, costs OpenAI tokens) vs scoped SQL re-tag of obvious cases. **Active queue post-this-entry:** ORCH-0700 SPEC dispatch BLOCKED on 5 operator decisions; > **2026-04-26 — ORCH-0685 cycle-2 FORENSICS RETURNED + REVIEW APPROVED → REFRAMED: Save IS technically working; toast feedback hidden behind RN Modal portal. SPEC DISPATCH BLOCKED on user picking fix shape.** Investigation: [reports/INVESTIGATION_ORCH-0685_cycle2_SAVE_DEAD_TAP.md](Mingla_Artifacts/reports/INVESTIGATION_ORCH-0685_cycle2_SAVE_DEAD_TAP.md). **Critical reframe: the Save isn't dead — the user's feedback channel is.** Tap path proven correct end-to-end (8 steps in §4 of report): button → handleSave → onSave(card) → handleSaveSharedCard → savedCardsService.saveCard → DB upsert. **Row IS being inserted in `saved_card`. Button DOES transition to "Saved" + filled-bookmark + disabled.** What's broken: success toast fired by `showNotification` is rendered into a sibling `<View>` of the chat-mounted `<ExpandedCardModal>` at [MessageInterface.tsx:1524-1547](app-mobile/src/components/MessageInterface.tsx#L1524-L1547). React Native's Modal creates a separate native window/overlay — sibling Views are rendered BEHIND it regardless of `zIndex: 50` or `elevation: 8` (RN's zIndex only operates within a single native window). Result: every toast pushed while modal is open is invisible to the user. They see the button transition (subtle) but no toast (their primary feedback signal) → "nothing happens." **Constitution #1 spirit violation, NOT letter** — button responds, save completes, only feedback hidden. **Findings tally:** 1 RC (proven HIGH from RN Modal docs + JSX sibling structure) + 2 CF (spec §9.4 assumed-without-verifying toast visibility; cycle-1 IMPL STEP X table covered field reads not feedback channels) + 2 HF (HF-1 ALL toasts from MessageInterface hidden behind ANY child modal — pre-existing pattern; HF-2 Alert.alert in ActionButtons line 215 unreachable because handleSaveSharedCard catches throws first) + 4 OBS (Save IS working; ORCH-0690 source-line confirmed at ActionButtons.tsx:251-255 + :309-313; TrackedTouchableOpacity not swallowing taps; currentUserId reliably defined). **3 fix shapes proposed** ranked by surgical-narrowness: Shape 1 (~5 LOC, replace `showNotification` with native `Alert.alert` for chat-mount Save — works definitively but intrusive UX); **Shape 2a (Recommended, ~15 LOC** — duplicate notifications panel inside chat-mount conditional in MessageInterface; existing panel stays for non-modal toasts; clean fix that addresses RC-1 only, doesn't touch other surfaces); > **2026-04-25 — ORCH-0678 INTAKE (S1 — Lagos seeded then Bouncer rejected 100% of rows).** User just seeded Lagos via admin-seed-places, ran run-bouncer, every place came back `is_servable=false`. > **2026-04-25 — ORCH-0668 IMPLEMENTOR RETURNED + REVIEW APPROVED (with spec deviation accepted) → TESTER DISPATCH READY.** Report: `outputs/IMPLEMENTATION_ORCH-0668_PAIRED_PROFILE_RPC_FIX_REPORT.md`. **Status: `implemented, partially verified`** — code, CI, invariant complete; migration apply + edge fn deploy + device smoke remain user-action-required per implementor "never deploy migrations" rule + DDL permission denial. **Spec deviation flagged in report §2 — orchestrator REVIEW ACCEPTS:** spec §4.1 SQL design (band_counts CTE + scalar subquery for "smallest qualifying band") failed perf gate at **46.9 s** for 11-signal Raleigh (sort spilled 707 MB to disk because `to_jsonb(pp.*)` was carried through DISTINCT ON sort). Implementor v2 redesign defers `to_jsonb` until AFTER `LIMIT 9` (only 9 hydrations vs 35 574) + uses `ORDER BY (band_idx ASC, signal_score DESC) LIMIT N` instead of band_counts InitPlan → **214.8 ms** at 11 signals (220× speedup). **Semantic difference acknowledged:** at urban locations (≥99% of users — Raleigh has 1797 places in band 1) result is identical; at rural locations where band 1 has < p_total_limit places, v2 prefers nearer-band candidates over higher-scored next-band candidates (a strict UX improvement vs legacy "smallest qualifying band only" policy). (Q4) "Could we see more" — quantify every artificial cap on the visible event horizon. **Pre-investigation code-review smells already noted (NOT verdicts — for forensics to confirm):** (a) `MUSIC_SEGMENT_ID` is hardcoded → UI title "Concerts & Events" ships sports/theatre/comedy/family/misc as zero — title is a lie; (b) **price tier chips** (`chill`/`comfy`/`bougie`/`lavish`) likely silent no-ops — the client-side filter switch only handles USD bands (`under-25`/`25-50`/`50-100`/`over-100`), tier IDs fall through to `default: return true`; (c) **genre keywords joined with comma** — `params.set("keyword", searchKeywords.join(","))` sends literal `"afrobeats,amapiano"` to TM, which is a phrase match not OR; suspect every non-`all` genre returns ~empty; (d) **AsyncStorage cache key omits the date filter** — switching `today → weekend` returns yesterday's `today` cache; (e) **edge-fn cache key uses only `startDate.slice(0,10)`** — endDate ignored, two date windows share a cache row; (f) **`countryCode` never sent to TM** + lat/lng radius=50km only — Lagos / Mumbai / São Paulo likely return zero with no UX distinction from "no events tonight"; (g) **`currency = range.currency ?? "USD"` falls back to USD** silently (Constitution #9/#10); (h) `formatDate` builds `Date.UTC(...)` from venue-local YYYY-MM-DD → day-of-week label may be wrong for AU/JP venues; (i) **price filter excludes TBA-price events invisibly** under any non-`any` chip (Constitution #3); (j) **page size 20, page 0 only, no pagination** → user-visible horizon ≤ 20; (k) sold-out events not filtered, just badged. **Severity S1** — primary content surface, multiple silent-failure paths, international correctness unverified, founder asked for brutal. Could escalate to S0 if Q1 live-fire shows non-US/UK markets get nothing. **Forensics dispatch:** [FORENSICS_ORCH-0670_CONCERTS_EVENTS_BRUTAL_AUDIT.md](Mingla_Artifacts/prompts/FORENSICS_ORCH-0670_CONCERTS_EVENTS_BRUTAL_AUDIT.md) — INVESTIGATE-ONLY, four-thread report (Q1 geography w/ ≥5-geo live-fire matrix mandatory per `feedback_headless_qa_rpc_gap.md`, Q2 per-filter H-grid w/ pass/fail/partial, Q3 silent-failure inventory, Q4 horizon caps with measurements), five-truth-layer reconcile, constitutional + invariant scan (#2/#3/#9/#10/#13 candidates), §0 founder-override clause if premise wrong, mandatory output to `reports/INVESTIGATION_ORCH-0670_CONCERTS_EVENTS.md`. ---

## User Journey

### Phase 1: Acquisition
Install → Welcome Screen → OAuth (Google/Apple)

### Phase 2: Onboarding
Phone OTP → Gender → Details → Value Prop → Intent → Location → Preferences → Friends → Collab → Consent → Deck Ready

### Phase 3: Core Loop
Explore (deck swipe) → Save → Schedule → Invite → Collaborate → Go → Review

### Phase 4: Retention
Calendar reminders → Push notifications → Holiday experiences → Re-engagement → Subscription upgrade

### Phase 5: Social
Friend discovery → Pair requests → DM → Map presence → Activity feed

| ORCH-0486 | Mixed-deck (category + curated) — category fetch failure silently absorbed when curated succeeds; AUTH_REQUIRED/PIPELINE_ERROR UI never fires | Discovery | P3 | quality-gap | awaiting-spec | F | — | Discovered by tester in ORCH-0474 cycle 0. When a deck has BOTH category pills AND curated pills, if `categoryPromise` rejects with `DeckFetchError` (auth-required or pipeline-error) while `curatedPromise` resolves, `deckService.fetchDeck` falls through to return curated-only cards with `serverPath` defaulting to `'pipeline'`. The tagged error discriminant is lost. User sees cards but no retry affordance for the failed category side. Fix is ~3 lines in `app-mobile/src/services/deckService.ts:fetchDeck` around line 482: even when curated succeeded, if `singlesResult.error instanceof DeckFetchError`, carry its `serverPath` into the final return. **Why low severity:** rare in practice — auth/pipeline failures typically hit both calls (same token, same backend), activating the existing "both failed" branch correctly. No crash, no security, no data loss. Not a blocker for ORCH-0474 cycle 1. |

| ORCH-0498 | Mixed-deck progressive-delivery double-wipe on solo pref change | Discovery | S1 | architecture-flaw | charter | F | — | Discovered 2026-04-18 via Phase 0-A amendment §12.2 (see `outputs/INVESTIGATION_ORCH-0485_DECK_PREF_CHANGE_LATENCY.md` §12). Solo analog of ORCH-0493 RC#1 — same disease, different trigger. Mechanism: on a MIXED deck (≥1 category + ≥1 curated pill), `onSinglesReady` in `useDeckCards.ts:148-162` writes `setQueryData(singles)` when singles resolve (~1s) → UI renders singles-only. User may start swiping. Later, full `fetchDeck` promise resolves with 1:1 interleaved `regular+curated` at `deckService.ts:484-503` — positions 0,1,2,3,4 become `reg[0], cur[0], reg[1], cur[1], reg[2]` instead of `reg[0..4]`. React Query overwrites cache. `recommendations` state changes. `SwipeableCards.tsx:979-980` sees first-5-IDs differ → WIPE #2: `setRemovedCards(new Set()) + setCurrentCardIndex(0)`. Any swipes in the singles-only window are lost. Occurs on EVERY solo user with curated pills on EVERY pref change. Confidence: H on mechanism (code-proven), M on user-visible outcome (depends on swipe timing; device test would confirm). Shares fix with ORCH-0491 + ORCH-0493 RC#1 (narrow "deck expanded, same session" signal vs full-replacement signal). Absorb into ORCH-0490 Phase 2.3 or dedicated slice — spec-writer call. |
| ORCH-0499 | `currentMode` + `currentSession` not persisted across cold launch — user always lands in Solo | Discovery + State & Cache | S1 | architecture-flaw | charter | F | — | Discovered 2026-04-18 via Phase 0-B `outputs/INVESTIGATION_ORCH-0492_PERSISTENCE_BASELINE.md` RC#2. Zustand partialize at `app-mobile/src/store/appStore.ts:206-216` intentionally EXCLUDES `isInSolo`, `currentSession`, `availableSessions`, `pendingInvites` — per comment at line 210-214: *"refreshed from the database on every app open"*. This was the correct design for ORCH-0209 (state survival) which optimized for freshness. JTBD-3 reframes the requirement: the user explicitly wants to resume the session they left. Default `isInSolo: true` at line 139 means every cold launch lands in Solo regardless of prior mode. Combined with ORCH-0492 RC#1 (`SwipeableCards.tsx:854-857` deletes prior-mode position on mode change) and ORCH-0492 RC#3 (`@mingla/lastDeckQueryKey` is solo-only), this is the third of three code sites that together block JTBD-3. Spec writer must balance freshness-vs-resumption tradeoff — likely by persisting mode+sessionId AND triggering validation re-fetch on resume (not either-or). Core of ORCH-0490 Phase 2.5. |
| ORCH-0500 | Dead React Query cache entries accumulate in persister after pref changes | State & Cache | S3 | quality-gap | open | F | — | Discovered 2026-04-18 via Phase 0-B HF#3. `REACT_QUERY_OFFLINE_CACHE` hydrates `deck-cards` entries regardless of whether `deckPrefsHash` in Zustand still matches. Pref change bumps `deckPrefsHash`, creates new query key — but OLD deck-cards entry under OLD key survives in the persisted blob. Dormant (new query uses new key), but consumes space toward the 1.5MB Android CursorWindow cap. Not critical today (fresh installs well under cap). Fix directions: prune entries not matching current `deckPrefsHash` on hydration, OR scope the persister to a single active key. Defer to post-ORCH-0490 unless the 1.5MB cap is hit in beta testing. |

| ORCH-0484 | 776 approved active places have `ai_categories = '{}'` (empty array) — should not exist per AI pipeline rules | Backend + Data Integrity | S2 | data-integrity | open | F | — | Discovered via ORCH-0480 implementor D-2 (2026-04-17), **tightened by tester 2026-04-17**: all 776 rows have `ai_categories = '{}'` (empty array), **ZERO are NULL**. Tester-verified correct count query: `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM place_pool WHERE is_active=true AND ai_approved=true AND COALESCE(array_length(ai_categories,1), 0) = 0` returns 776 on Mingla-dev. (Implementor's report used `array_length=0` which returns NULL for empty arrays, not TRUE — same Postgres NULL-semantics gotcha tricked tester initially too.) These rows are correctly excluded from ORCH-0480's new partial index (predicate `array_length(ai_categories,1) > 0` correctly fails for empty arrays), so no perf impact. But their existence contradicts the AI pipeline contract (approval requires category assignment). Need investigator to trace — legacy pre-AI rows, race condition in ai-verify-pipeline, or silent failure in validation writeback. Pair with ORCH-0481 MV migration (clean up before snapshot). |
| ORCH-0487 | admin_place_city_overview <500ms target not met — residual Bitmap Heap Scan I/O on Mingla-dev after ORCH-0481 rework | Admin + Backend | S2 | performance | open | F | — | Registered 2026-04-17 from ORCH-0481 rework cycle 1 D-NEW-1. Post-rework timing on Mingla-dev: **3,061ms warm** (down from 5,118ms pre-rework). Under PostgREST 8s timeout so the admin country-drill-down page loads, but 6× over the <500ms spec target. Root cause: Bitmap Heap Scan on 4,858 MV heap pages for a single country's ~31k rows (columns `has_photos`, `primary_category`, `rating`, `city_id` are not in the existing `(country_code, is_active, ai_approved)` index, forcing heap access for projection). Fix: follow-up migration adding `INCLUDE (city_id, has_photos, primary_category, rating)` to `admin_place_pool_mv_country_active_approved` index (enables Index-Only Scan; expected <200ms). Alternative: CLUSTER the MV by country_code (one-time heap reorganization). Not blocking admin dashboard load today; defer until ORCH-0481 cycle 1 closes + city-drill-down UX feedback confirms the 3s latency matters. |
| ORCH-0488 | Admin RPC cache-sensitivity on Mingla-dev — 2-5s cold-cache latencies across multiple admin_* RPCs (not just city_overview) | Admin + Backend | S2 | performance | open | F | — | Registered 2026-04-17 from ORCH-0481 tester cycle 1 retest D-NEW-6. Tester observed: `admin_place_country_overview` 87ms hot / 5,047ms mildly-cold / 6,832ms fully-cold; `admin_place_category_breakdown` 107ms cycle 0 / 4,219ms cycle 1 (unchanged body — plan drift + cold cache). Root cause: Mingla-dev's slow I/O (~1ms per heap page read) means the 44MB MV (27 cols × 63k rows) exceeds shared_buffers working set. When pages get evicted between queries, re-reads are I/O-bound. **Decision point: is this Mingla-dev-only or does it replicate on production?** Production may have larger shared_buffers / faster disk → cache hit ratios closer to 100% → sub-500ms consistently. **Defer evaluation until post-production deploy.** If prod also sees 2-5s latencies, the structural fix is to narrow the MV (drop TOAST'd columns like `stored_photo_urls raw`, `photos jsonb`, `ai_categories raw`, `types raw` that only a few RPCs need — reduces physical footprint ~10× to 4-5MB, fits in cache). Not blocking close if admin page loads under 8s. |
| ORCH-0489 | Admin UI "Refresh Stats" button — replaces failed pg_cron auto-refresh with user-controlled refresh | Admin UI | S1 | missing-feature | **implemented-awaiting-verify** | F | — | Implementation delivered 2026-04-18 by implementor: single-file change in `mingla-admin/src/pages/PlacePoolManagementPage.jsx`, ~35 lines added (state + handler + Button JSX) inside `OverviewTab`. Build-verified (`npm run build` PASS: 2918 modules, 0 errors, 11.93s). Report: `reports/IMPLEMENTATION_ORCH-0489_ADMIN_REFRESH_BUTTON_REPORT.md`. Structural review APPROVED — Button placed right-aligned in new flex header row next to scope label; calls `supabase.rpc('admin_refresh_place_pool_mv')`; auth-error path via `/not authorized/i` regex surfaces "Admin access required" toast; success path shows row count + duration, auto-refires `fetchData()`; `mountedRef.current` guard for unmount safety. All 8 SCs met by construction or build. **Awaiting runtime verification** (prompt: `prompts/TESTER_ORCH-0489_ADMIN_REFRESH_BUTTON.md`) — 6 browser-driven checks (visual render, click flow, auth-error path, long-running refresh, regression in other tabs, MV actually refreshes). On tester PASS → ORCH-0489 closes A and ORCH-0481 promotes D→A. |
